    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }

      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app',

<span id="freeTextContainer14372423200179741858">In a heartwarming novel that is destined to become a Christmas classic, acclaimed author Elvira Woodruff tells the story of two orphaned sisters whose lives are forever changed by a magical doll.<br/><br/>Lucy and Glory are orphaned sisters with no real place to call home.   <span id="freeText14372423200179741858" style="display:none">In a heartwarming novel that is destined to become a Christmas classic, acclaimed author Elvira Woodruff tells the story of two orphaned sisters whose lives are forever changed by a magical doll.<br /><br />Lucy and Glory are orphaned sisters with no real place to call home. Only their memories of a beautiful doll named Morning Glory brighten their bleak lives. When a deadly fever sweeps through the workhouse where the girls live, Lucy and Glory flee to the mean streets of London.<br />One day the girls find an old battered doll that Glory senses is their beloved Morning Glory. But Morning Glory is no ordinary doll--the girls learn that she has magical powers that will change their lives in amazing ways.. With the help of the doll, the sisters discover the true meaning of the Christmas spirit.</span>

<div id="review_1124670640" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1124670640" />
    <a title="Manybooks" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2970379-manybooks"><img alt="Manybooks" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1459773375p2/2970379.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1124670640?book_show_action=true">Dec 06, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Manybooks" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Manybooks" href="/user/show/2970379-manybooks">Manybooks</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">children who enjoy too-good-to-be-true Christmas tales, or doll tales</span></div>

        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2970379-manybooks?shelf=four-seasons-winter">four-seasons-winter</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2970379-manybooks?shelf=childrens-literature">childrens-literature</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2970379-manybooks?shelf=book-reviews">book-reviews</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2970379-manybooks?shelf=doll-fiction">doll-fiction</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1124670640" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1873233889249297248">While many if not most of the general themes of this slight little story, of Elvira Woodruff's <u>The Christmas Doll</u> are indeed interesting enough, and while it does paint a generally realistic enough picture of poverty and workhouse conditions of/in late 19th century London, the story itself is just much too melodramatic and implausible for my own personal tastes. For the painful and heartbreaking reality of the two orphaned sisters' in all ways massively desperate plight is in my humble opinion r</span>
  <span id="freeText1873233889249297248" style="display:none">While many if not most of the general themes of this slight little story, of Elvira Woodruff's <u>The Christmas Doll</u> are indeed interesting enough, and while it does paint a generally realistic enough picture of poverty and workhouse conditions of/in late 19th century London, the story itself is just much too melodramatic and implausible for my own personal tastes. For the painful and heartbreaking reality of the two orphaned sisters' in all ways massively desperate plight is in my humble opinion rather trivialised and with that also much diluted by the fact that they very smoothly and seamlessly manage to escape from the workhouse, almost immediately find a trusty friend and then of course a sympathetic doll-making spinster to adopt them (and thus <u>The Christmas Doll</u> feels more like one is reading a fantasy, a fairy tale, than reality, and while I do think that author Elvira Woodruff actually seems to consider her story as a piece of reality, perhaps feel-good reality, but reality all the same, personally, I simply cannot see and feel this all that much myself). That being said, I was still considering ranking <u>The Christmas Doll</u> with a low three star rating until I stumbled upon the epilogue (which is not only saccharine sweet to the extreme and even more implausible than the main body of the narrative, but also reads at least to me, as something more akin and alike to a homily or church sermon). And thus, while <u>The Christmas Doll</u> might well be of interest and enjoyable to those who like so-called doll fiction and totally feel-good Christmas stories, for a tale that on the surface appears to strive to be realistic, to and for me, <u>The Christmas Doll</u> is simply much too sugar-coated, too good to be true to be more than a two star reading experience at best.</span>
  <a data-text-id="1873233889249297248" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1763357392" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1763357392" />
    <a title="Hilary" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/42315986-hilary"><img alt="Hilary" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1445715101p2/42315986.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1763357392?book_show_action=true">Dec 19, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Hilary" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Hilary" href="/user/show/42315986-hilary">Hilary</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">Readers who like christmas stories, books about orphans and dolls</span></div>

        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/42315986-hilary?shelf=female-author-or-illustrator">female-author-or-illustrator</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/42315986-hilary?shelf=doll-stories">doll-stories</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/42315986-hilary?shelf=christmas-books">christmas-books</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/42315986-hilary?shelf=orphan-stories">orphan-stories</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1763357392" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12642130768077373015">Read aloud to my daughter, I would perhaps rate 3 but she thought nearer 4 stars. This book had all the ingredients we love for a story, orphans, escape from cruel orphanage, dolls, christmas, happy ending etc, but it was so short, and events happened in a quick and predictable way. The escape from the orphanage was decided and then they escaped. We would have liked to have been on the edge of our seats a bit, enjoying their planning and wondering if they would make it. There are some parts wher</span>
  <span id="freeText12642130768077373015" style="display:none">Read aloud to my daughter, I would perhaps rate 3 but she thought nearer 4 stars. This book had all the ingredients we love for a story, orphans, escape from cruel orphanage, dolls, christmas, happy ending etc, but it was so short, and events happened in a quick and predictable way. The escape from the orphanage was decided and then they escaped. We would have liked to have been on the edge of our seats a bit, enjoying their planning and wondering if they would make it. There are some parts where the girls act selflessly that are unrealistic and bordering on the nauseating. There were some historical inaccuracies and I was suprised that someone called someone else a tosspot, I can only assume this has a different meaning in the US !<br /><br />This book felt like it was a rough draft of what could be quite a fun story, but really needed filling out with lots more detail and day to day life. We liked the idea of the doll shop though and lots of reviews are really positive about this book. </span>

          </span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer251766577" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16259247676980407128">My daughter told me I should read this book last year when I was doing the Christmas Spirit Reading Challenge, but I never got to it. So, I decided to read it this year. It is the story of two orphan girls who escape the workhouse and live on the streets in the city. The elder, Lucy, got a job at a doll's shop when she went in to try to sell a doll she had found in the mud. She happened to be wearing her sister Glory's apron upon which she had stitched a little Morning Glory flower. The shopkeep</span>
  <span id="freeText16259247676980407128" style="display:none">My daughter told me I should read this book last year when I was doing the Christmas Spirit Reading Challenge, but I never got to it. So, I decided to read it this year. It is the story of two orphan girls who escape the workhouse and live on the streets in the city. The elder, Lucy, got a job at a doll's shop when she went in to try to sell a doll she had found in the mud. She happened to be wearing her sister Glory's apron upon which she had stitched a little Morning Glory flower. The shopkeeper noticed the flower and was convinced that Lucy had talent for stitching and could be their Hearts Girl for the Christmas season. I know I have told a bit about the story, but there is so much more to tell. It's a sad, but sweet story about the sisters' love for each other and the hope that kept them alive. I know it is a children's book, but it was such a satisfying read for this Christmas season. </span>
  <a data-text-id="16259247676980407128" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_134563531" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/134563531" />
    <a title="Donna" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4633421-donna"><img alt="Donna" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/f_50x66-6a03a5c12233c941481992b82eea8d23.png" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/134563531?book_show_action=true">Dec 11, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Donna" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Donna" href="/user/show/4633421-donna">Donna</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer134563531" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16186076804152879418">The Christmas Doll is a story about two orphans who were being brought to a factory and were forced to work there. It's setting is in London, where the time is 150 years ago, and it was a very dark society at that time. The were sisters, and everyday the factory they had very less food to eat, and the quality of the food is very poor. Then the younger sister got sick and was being separated from her sister. And this led to the escape of the two sisters from the factory. After the escape they had</span>
  <span id="freeText16186076804152879418" style="display:none">The Christmas Doll is a story about two orphans who were being brought to a factory and were forced to work there. It's setting is in London, where the time is 150 years ago, and it was a very dark society at that time. The were sisters, and everyday the factory they had very less food to eat, and the quality of the food is very poor. Then the younger sister got sick and was being separated from her sister. And this led to the escape of the two sisters from the factory. After the escape they had to survive on their own, and really quickly, the older sister had found a job in a doll shop, where the owner is very nice to her, and she gets to sleep in the shop over night, then at night she would just invite her young sister in and in the day time her younger sister would stay on the streets. <br /><br />I think this is a really touching story, where the older sister always takes care of the younger one, and never gives up on her. The story is called the christmas doll because before the two sister's parents died they used to own a doll and this doll was what kept them alive and they would want to find it again, because they lost it when being forced to work in the factory. Soon they found it in the older sister's doll shop, and that why the story is called the christmas doll. <br /><br />I learned a lot from this story, where I got to know no matter how hard life is, we should never give up, and also never give up on the people around you. I think this book is really good, and I really enjoyed it, I would highly recommend this book to the people around me. </span>
  <a data-text-id="16186076804152879418" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1835201369" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1835201369" />
    <a title="Clare" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1056629-clare"><img alt="Clare" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1219068471p2/1056629.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1835201369?book_show_action=true">Dec 16, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Clare" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Clare" href="/user/show/1056629-clare">Clare</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1056629-clare?shelf=fiction">fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1056629-clare?shelf=childrens">childrens</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1056629-clare?shelf=christmas">christmas</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1835201369" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4430017782578951497">This tender story takes place in mid 1800's London where two orphaned sisters escape from the workhouse where they lived to try to make it on their own. London back then was not a kind place for those down on their luck, but Lucy, the older sister is determined to keep her little sister Glory safe even in the desperate situation in which they now find themselves. </span>

          </span>

  <span id="freeText9014711810269543790" style="display:none">Yes, yes, a thousand times yes. I'd give this book 10 stars if I could.<br /><br />(Some of the reviews on here make me laugh because they have nothing to do with the book itself. But if you're of sound mind, and are interested in this as a book to read, please proceed. If not, there are plenty of skewered "reviews" on here judging it for being too bleak or not about Christ in Christmas. LOLZ)<br /><br />This book appealed to me because of the bleak, Victorian circumstances of the girls and the realistic portrayals of poverty, and how joyful the smallest kindness can be interpreted. <br /><br />I'd say this one is too dark for children, but I would have read it (and loved it). Then again, I was into Edward Gorey and Tim Burton at age 7, so there you go. This one was right up my (dark) alley and I wish I could have read it sooner. This is one of my favorites now, and it definitely will be reread at Christmastime. It will, however, tug on sensitive heartstrings, so be aware of that.<br /><br />If you're in to dark tales of stories involving the Victorian era, doll shops, almshouses, illnesses taking over entire cities, sisters saving each other, death occurring at a young age, or something new for Christmas, give this one a try. I'm glad I did. <br /><br />I love this book. LOVE IT.</span>

<div id="review_2960192510" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2960192510" />
    <a title="Gale" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/17664194-gale"><img alt="Gale" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1370880898p2/17664194.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">

        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2960192510?book_show_action=true">Sep 01, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Gale" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Gale" href="/user/show/17664194-gale">Gale</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2960192510" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16163934493347025867"> “Secrets of the Human and a Doll’s Heart”<br/><br/> Set in Victorian England under conditions straight out of Dickens, this story presents a grim depiction of life in a London workhouse (cruel places to remove poor orphans from polite society’s view) and on the streets. Sisters Lucy and little Glory, fearing dreaded separation, risk everything to escape their callous existence at Grimstone—an apt description of the “home.” But survival on the streets and back alleys of London proves dangerous as well, un</span>
  <span id="freeText16163934493347025867" style="display:none"> “Secrets of the Human and a Doll’s Heart”<br /><br /> Set in Victorian England under conditions straight out of Dickens, this story presents a grim depiction of life in a London workhouse (cruel places to remove poor orphans from polite society’s view) and on the streets. Sisters Lucy and little Glory, fearing dreaded separation, risk everything to escape their callous existence at Grimstone—an apt description of the “home.” But survival on the streets and back alleys of London proves dangerous as well, until they are befriended by a street-wise boy named Nick. Pooling their meager talents they plan to sponge off the relative comforts of Thimblebee’s Doll Shop.<br /><br /> So much for the plot; the real treasure of this story is revealed by various themes of the heart—both human and that of a doll. Lucy is a skilled little seamstress, but it is her sickly little sister—clinging to memories of their lost Christmas childhood--who teaches them all the true meaning of Christmas sacrifice. Despite the delicately sentimental denouements this book tugs at the heartstrings. For girls of all ages--whoever loved a doll.<br /><br /> September 1, 2019<br /> <br /></span>

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5185313-debra?shelf=juvenile">juvenile</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2630282641" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9071181101746355714"> A touching story about a very bleak time for orphaned children in Victorian England. I have always enjoyed the books of Elivira Woodruff and I wanted a Christmas book to add to my holiday enjoyment. This started out very sadly, much in the mood of Dickens' A Christmas Carol, and only got sadder as the two little sisters escaped from the workhouse to avoid the spreading sickness that was killing off several children a day. The introduction of several kindnesses of strangers and their muck diggin</span>
  <span id="freeText9071181101746355714" style="display:none"> A touching story about a very bleak time for orphaned children in Victorian England. I have always enjoyed the books of Elivira Woodruff and I wanted a Christmas book to add to my holiday enjoyment. This started out very sadly, much in the mood of Dickens' A Christmas Carol, and only got sadder as the two little sisters escaped from the workhouse to avoid the spreading sickness that was killing off several children a day. The introduction of several kindnesses of strangers and their muck digging unearthing a porcelain headed doll turned the story. The entrance of Nick Button, an enterprising young man, who befriended them and shared his meager food and earnings, as well as his street smarts, was uplifting. The relentless hope and cheer from the little girls was wonderful. I know it is very predictable, but it is Christmas and I enjoyed the warm ending.</span>
  <a data-text-id="9071181101746355714" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<span id="freeTextContainer9193655482274190593">This was a cute story and I can tell I would have loved it when I was a child. There was a stark contrast throughout the book though.   <span id="freeText9193655482274190593" style="display:none">This was a cute story and I can tell I would have loved it when I was a child. There was a stark contrast throughout the book though. There were descriptions of what life was like for orphaned children in Victorian England, including multiple cases of death. Somehow, though, the story was almost sickeningly sweet. I'm not sure if it was the characterizations or the plotline, but it really soften the harshness of the girls' situations. <br /><br />Still, I'm 29, and this book wasn't written for me. I can still read books with the perspective I had when I was younger, and as I said before, I know I would have loved this when I was in elementary school. It's a lovely story about family and staying true to your own standards of decency and kindness under terrible circumstances.</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer16773259367563088496">This story seems to me to be a hybrid of a Charles Dickens/George MacDonald tale... It's about two little orphans who run away from the workhouse and end up on the streets of London. I did like the relationship the two sisters had, and the boy they meet is a fun addition. I love the element of the doll-maker, so that was definitely a bonus for me.<br/><br/>In many ways, the story isn't terribly realistic. It almost has a fairy tale quality to it. However, if you know that going in, you can enjoy it for wh</span>
  <span id="freeText16773259367563088496" style="display:none">This story seems to me to be a hybrid of a Charles Dickens/George MacDonald tale... It's about two little orphans who run away from the workhouse and end up on the streets of London. I did like the relationship the two sisters had, and the boy they meet is a fun addition. I love the element of the doll-maker, so that was definitely a bonus for me.<br /><br />In many ways, the story isn't terribly realistic. It almost has a fairy tale quality to it. However, if you know that going in, you can enjoy it for what it is. A very nice Christmas story with a sweet and happy ending. </span>

<div id="review_1614149324" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1614149324" />
    <a title="Jessica Riben" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/52056234-jessica-riben"><img alt="Jessica Riben" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/f_50x66-6a03a5c12233c941481992b82eea8d23.png" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1614149324?book_show_action=true">Apr 18, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jessica Riben" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jessica Riben" href="/user/show/52056234-jessica-riben">Jessica Riben</a>
      </span>

          added it




        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1614149324" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10729423442669695365"><b>Title</b>: The Christmas Doll<br/><b>Author</b>: Elvira Woodruff<br/><b>Illustrator</b>: N/A<br/><b>Genre</b>: Historical Fiction<br/><b>Theme(s)</b>: Orphans, Christmas, Dolls<br/><b>Opening line/sentence</b>: Long ago in London Town, at a time when the muffin man’s cries began the day, and the lamplighter ushered in the night, two young girls lived together in the bleak, cold shelter of a public workhouse.<br/><b>Brief Book Summary</b>: Lucy and Glory are two orphaned sisters who have no place to call home. One day they escape and are on the streets of London to fend </span>
  <span id="freeText10729423442669695365" style="display:none"><b>Title</b>: The Christmas Doll<br /><b>Author</b>: Elvira Woodruff<br /><b>Illustrator</b>: N/A<br /><b>Genre</b>: Historical Fiction<br /><b>Theme(s)</b>: Orphans, Christmas, Dolls<br /><b>Opening line/sentence</b>: Long ago in London Town, at a time when the muffin man’s cries began the day, and the lamplighter ushered in the night, two young girls lived together in the bleak, cold shelter of a public workhouse.<br /><b>Brief Book Summary</b>: Lucy and Glory are two orphaned sisters who have no place to call home. One day they escape and are on the streets of London to fend for themselves. Then one day the girls discover an old battered doll that they find out has magical powers. This doll shows the girls what it means to have the Christmas Spirit.<br /><b>Professional Recommendation/Review #1</b>: Kirkus (Kirkus Reviews, October 15, 2000 (Vol. 68, No. 20)) <br />Imagine that 150 years ago, Charles Dickens decided to write a book just for little girls: a touching tale of not one but two deserving orphans, runaways from the workhouse who are starving in the teaming streets of Victorian London. Through luck, pluck, and assorted amazing coincidences, they find a streetwise older boy (an honest version of the Artful Dodger) to help them and a kindly doll-shop owner, Miss Thimblebee, who gives the oldest sister a job and eventually provides a loving home for both girls. Dickens, of course, never wrote a tale of two sisters, but Woodruff ("George Washington's Socks", 1999, etc.) has spun just such a magical story, expertly incorporating a dash of Dickens with extensive historical research in the early Victorian era into her well-crafted plot. Ten-year-old Lucy and her six-year-old sister Glory are desperately trying to survive in the crowded slums of London when they find an old doll in the mud next to the Thames River. The plot turns on this particular doll, which is sold for a penny, later refurbished in the doll shop, and then chosen as the Christmas doll for the ailing daughter of Queen Victoria's gardener. The story is told in short chapters with the author employing another Dickensian device--much cliffhanging chapter endings. Young readers who like the American Girls and Dear America series will enjoy this fast-paced historical novel, and mothers or grandmothers will enjoy reading it to girls too young to read by themselves. A "dollightful" surprise for Santa to tuck under the Christmas tree . . . perhaps in the arms of an old-fashioned doll. 2000, Scholastic, $15.95. Category: Fiction. Ages 6 to 11. Starred Review. © 2000 Kirkus Reviews/VNU eMedia, Inc. All rights reserved. <br />(PUBLISHER: Scholastic 151p $15.95., PUBLISHED: 2000)<br /><b>Professional Recommendation/Review #2</b>: Wende Sairio (Audiofile, December/January 2007) <br />Long ago London was a terrifying place. Worrying about danger, illness, and getting caught and returned to the orphanage, Lucy must protect and provide for her sister, Glory. But it's the loving stories and gentle magic of the doll, Morning Glory, that have kept them both alive and hopeful. Although the characters are simple, the story's plot is appropriately suspenseful and predictably satisfying. Bernadette Dunne's narration is solid, making the characters real. Dunne's versatility, as she ably differentiates the characters, highlights the extremes of poverty and wealth in the lives of the different social classes and leaves the reader with a warm, hopeful feeling. W.L.S. (c) AudioFile 2006, Portland, Maine Unabridged. 2005 (orig. 2000), Blackstone Audiobooks, Three cassettes, 3 hrs., Library Ed., $44.95, Three CDs, $55.00. Ages 10 up. <br />(PUBLISHER: Blackstone Audiobooks Three cassettes 3 hrs. Library Ed. $44.95 Three CDs $55.00., PUBLISHED: 2005 (orig. 2000))<br /><b>Response to Two Professional Reviews</b>: <br />Both of these reviews explain that Lucy and Glory are orphans who escaped, and are not in a bad area in London. The first review relates this book to Charles Dickens, asking us to imagine he wrote a book just for girls, wondering how the story would play out. She also says that young girls who like American Girl Dolls would be attracted to this book. The second review tells us how magical the story is and how an old doll kept the orphan sisters both alive and hopeful. <br /><b>Evaluation of Literary Elements</b>: <br />This book shows students how young children like that had to live and survive back in the day. It explains what it means to be an orphan and how their lives are much different, learning to fend for themselves. It also gives the impression that these girls have magical talent, but in the end, they are just bringing out the spirit of Christmas. The book is broken up into short chapters so it is easy for young children to follow along. <br /><b>Consideration of Instructional Application</b>: <br />This book is geared more towards girls because all the main characters are girls and they are playing with dolls. For this book, students can come up with a creative writing piece about themselves encountering a magical person or creature. The students would tell us who the person or creature is, where they met it, and what adventures and activities they would have with their magical friend. Then students could share their stories with other students and see if they have similar magical friends and similar adventures they would go on. </span>
  <a data-text-id="10729423442669695365" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2197078771" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16351240523946156783">An orphan story about 2 sisters, lost doll and a found doll, no home to finding a home. Sad at times and hopeful at the end. may be a bit sappy but would be a nice story to read with your kids with a lesson on kindness and giving of yourself.<br/><br/>Bernadette Dunne's narration was great, every character had their own voice and emotion, which was important in this story.<br/><br/>Nice Christmas story!</span>

          </span>
        </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2200122267" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13239097940531904986">Syrupy sweet, predictable and great frothy fun for the Christmas season. From the very first sentence you hope (and know) that Lucy and Glory are going to survive the mean streets of London and connect with a perfect doll. This could become a household staple like Rumer Godden's The Story Of Holly and Ivy, which I've loved since I was a little girl.</span>

          </span>

//<![CDATA[  

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('TjDMFX6p3TdsZK2dr1NGiDyEj6NI1JEv4/tEnJrSADejR5nV6jRh46vgZVmtfdbp+aUn557FTmLjgJTsyCUxfw==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('u6v7OeZsn1nMBonHX1VVmgqko4JolI8427QRcuRCozZW3K75cvEjjQuCQQNde8X7z4ULxr6FUHXbz8ECtrWSfg==')})
  }
//]]>
</script>

      <div id="aboutAuthor" class=" clearFloats bigBox"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground"><a href="/author/show/4355.Elvira_Woodruff">About Elvira Woodruff</a></h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent">
          <div class='bookAuthorProfile'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__topContainer'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__photoContainer'>
<a href="/author/show/4355.Elvira_Woodruff"><div class='bookAuthorProfile__photo' style='background-image: url(https://images.gr-assets.com/authors/1291698284p3/4355.jpg);'></div>
</a></div>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__widgetContainer'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__name'>
<a href="/author/show/4355.Elvira_Woodruff">Elvira Woodruff
</a></div>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__followerCount'>
57
followers
</div>

</div>
</div>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer17328451669056485874">Well-known for her popular children’s stories, author Elvira Woodruff had a long route to becoming a writer. In fact, one of her first jobs after leaving college was driving an ice cream truck. She has also worked as a receptionist, a janitor, a window dresser, a gardener, a shop owner, an assistant librarian, a waitress, and a storyteller. After working for several years in the children’s room of</span>
  <span id="freeText17328451669056485874" style="display:none">Well-known for her popular children’s stories, author Elvira Woodruff had a long route to becoming a writer. In fact, one of her first jobs after leaving college was driving an ice cream truck. She has also worked as a receptionist, a janitor, a window dresser, a gardener, a shop owner, an assistant librarian, a waitress, and a storyteller. After working for several years in the children’s room of a library, Woodruff began writing professionally at the age of 35, and hasn’t stopped since.<br /><br />Elvira Woodruff has always had a great imagination. She recalls, “my father was a truck driver and I would love to sit in his truck and imagine all the places he’d been. I’d sit behind the wheel, my head barely reaching the steering wheel and pretend that I was on the open road, off on some grand adventure to faraway places like Long Island, or Jersey City.”<br /><br />Today, Woodruff believes that “what you have to do as a writer is to feel, look, and listen. Your stories then become a celebration of those observations. And, most important, a writer needs to fall in love. I’m constantly falling in love—with colors, with flowers, with wings, with bubbles, with mud, with goofy baby smiles. . . . When you’re writing under the influence of love, there’s a power that will weave your words into magic.”<br /><br />Born and raised in New Jersey, Elvira Woodruff has also lived in Boston, Massachusetts. She has two sons, Noah and Jess. When she isn’t writing, Woodruff likes gardening—especially with blue flowers—and enjoys traveling. “[One] year I fell in love with Leonardo daVinci and flew to Italy where I rented a car and traced his footsteps from Vinci to Florence and Milan.” She also spends a lot of her time visiting schools and libraries, sharing her ideas about writing with children.<br /><br />Elvira Woodruff’s book, Dear Napoleon, I Know You’re Dead, But . . ., is a clever and funny story about a boy who writes a letter to Napoleon Bonaparte for a class project, and receives a surprising reply. It has been included in numerous child-voted state award programs, including the Mark Twain Book Award program (Missouri), the Sequoyah Children’s Book Award program (Oklahoma), and the West Virginia Children’s Book Award program.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="17328451669056485874" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>
